This cover page and the inside cover page contain certain information for general reference only. They are not intended 
to be a summary of the security or terms of this issue. Investors are advised to read this entire Official Statement to obtain 
information essential to making an informed investment decision. Capitalized terms used on this cover page not otherwise 
defined shall have the meanings set forth herein.
The City of Joliet, Illinois (the “City”), owns and operates a waterworks system and a sanitary sewerage system as a 
combined utility system (the “System”). The City is issuing its Waterworks and Sewerage Senior Lien Revenue Bonds, Series 
2025 (the “Bonds”) for the purpose of (i) financing capital improvements to provide for the transmission to the System of Lake 
Michigan water pursuant to a water purchase agreement with the City of Chicago and the design, engineering, acquisition, 
construction and installation of a water transmission main and delivery system to interconnect the facilities of the Chicago 
water system with the water distribution facilities of the System (the “Water Transmission System Project”), (ii) making 
a deposit to the Common Debt Service Reserve Sub-Fund and (iii) paying costs of issuance of the Bonds. The proceeds 
of the Bonds will be used for System improvements such as elevated and standpipe water tanks, water pumping stations, 
transmission and distribution mains, and operations and administrative facilities for the System.
The Bonds will be issued as fully registered bonds and, when issued, will be registered in the name of Cede & Co., as 
nominee for The Depository Trust Company, New York, New York (“DTC”). DTC will act as securities depository for the 
Bonds. Purchases of beneficial ownership interests in the Bonds will be made in book-entry only form, in denominations of 
$5,000 principal amount and integral multiples thereof. Purchasers will not receive certificates representing their ownership 
interest in the Bonds purchased. Principal and interest on the Bonds will be paid directly to DTC by U.S. Bank Trust Company, 
National Association, Chicago, Illinois, appointed as Trustee under the Master Trust Indenture and as the Paying Agent (the 
“Paying Agent,” “Bond Registrar,” and “Trustee”) for the Bonds. Interest on the Bonds will be payable semi-annually on each 
January 1 and July 1, commencing July 1, 2026.
The Bonds are subject to redemption prior to maturity in the manner, on the dates and at the redemption price described 
under “
The  Bonds  – RedempTion  pRioR  To  m aTuRiTy ” herein.
The Bonds are limited obligations of the City payable from the Revenues (as defined in the Master Indenture) of the 
System and certain other moneys and securities held by the Trustee under the Master Indenture and the Second Supplemental 
Indenture. The Bonds shall not constitute an indebtedness or a loan of the credit of the City within the meaning of any 
constitutional or statutory limitation and neither the full faith and credit nor the taxing power of the City is pledged to the 
payment of the principal of or the interest on the Bonds. Pursuant to the Master Indenture, the Bonds are Senior Lien Obligations 
and shall be payable from, and secured by a pledge of, lien on and security interest in the Trust Estate consisting of (i) the 
Revenues, (ii) amounts on deposit in the Funds, Accounts and Dedicated Sub-Funds established under the Master Indenture 
and the Second Supplemental Indenture and (iii) all other moneys held from time to time under the Master Indenture and the 
Second Supplemental Indenture for the payment of the Bonds. See “
s ecuRiTy  foR  The  Bonds ” herein.
The scheduled payment of principal of and interest on the Bonds when due will be guaranteed under a municipal bond 
insurance policy to be issued concurrently with the delivery of the Bonds by BUILD AMERICA MUTUAL ASSURANCE 
COMPANY.

CITY OF JOLIET, ILLINOIS 
$109,835,000 
Waterworks and Sewerage Senior Lien Revenue Bonds, Series 2025 
INTRODUCTION 
The $109,835,000 Waterworks and Sewerage Senior Lien Revenue Bonds, Series 2025 
(the "Bonds"), are being issued pursuant to the home rule powers of the City of Joliet, Illinois (the 
"City"), under Section 6, Article VII of the 1970 Constitution of the State of Illinois. The Bonds 
are authorized by an ordinance adopted by the City Council of the City on the 3rd day of June, 
2025 (the "Ordinance"), the Master Indenture of Trust Securing Waterworks and Sewerage 
Revenue Senior Lien Obligations dated March 15, 2022 (the "Master Trust Indenture") from the 
City to U.S. Bank Trust Company, National Association, as trustee (the "Paying Agent," "Bond 
Registrar" and "Trustee") and the Second Supplemental Indenture from the City to the Trustee 
dated as of December 1, 2025 (the "Second Supplemental Indenture" and together with the Master 
Trust Indenture, the "Indenture") authorized therein and executed in connection with the sale of 
the Bonds. 
The City owns and operates a waterworks system and a sanitary sewerage system as a 
combined utility system (the "System"). Bond proceeds will be used for the purpose of (i) financing 
capital improvements to provide for the transmission to the System of Lake Michigan water 
pursuant to a water purchase agreement with the City of Chicago and the design, engineering, 
acquisition, construction and installation of a water transmission main and delivery system to 
interconnect the facilities of the Chicago water system with the water distribution facilities of the 
System (the "Water Transmission System Project"), (ii) making a deposit to the Common Debt 
Service Reserve Sub-Fund and (iii) paying costs of issuance of the Bonds. The proceeds of the 
Bonds will be used for System improvements such as elevated and standpipe water tanks, water 
pumping stations, transmission and distribution mains, and operations and administrative facilities 
for the System. The City is also undertaking a System wide program for the design, engineering, 
acquisition, construction and installation of new water mains, the rehabilitation of existing water 
mains and related improvements (the "Water Main Replacement Project" and together with the 
Water Transmission System Project, the "Project").  
The City has entered into agreements with the United States Environmental Protection 
Agency ("USEPA") pursuant to the Water Infrastructure Finance and Innovation Act ("WIFIA") 
to fund certain costs of the Project. The City has posted the WIFIA Master Agreement and the 
WIFIA Loan Agreements to the Electronic Municipal Market Access system ("EMMA"). 
The System includes all property, real, personal or otherwise owned or to be owned by the 
City or under control of the City, and used for waterworks and sewerage purposes, and any and all 
further extensions, improvements and additions thereto. The Bonds and all other Senior Lien 
Obligations are payable from "Revenues" (as defined in the Indenture) and certain other moneys 
and securities held by the Trustee under the provisions of the Indenture.   
2 
 
SYSTEM FUNDS 
There is maintained under the Indenture the Waterworks and Sewerage Fund which is an 
enterprise fund of the City. The Indenture also creates the Operation and Maintenance Fund and 
the System General Fund which are held and maintained by the City. The Indenture also creates 
as special funds of the City the Revenue Fund, the Debt Service Fund, the Junior Lien Obligation 
Debt Service Fund and the Renewal and Replacement Fund which are held by the Trustee. The 
Common Debt Service Reserve Sub-Fund is established as a Dedicated Sub-Fund within the Debt 
Service Fund which is also held by the Trustee. Defined terms not otherwise defined herein have 
the meanings as set forth in the Indenture. See  APPENDIX E - SUMMARY OF CERTAIN 
PROVISIONS OF THE INDENTURE hereto. 
All Revenues shall be collected by the City and each month, prior to the tenth day of the 
month, the City shall (i) apply the Revenues to increase the amount then held in the Operation and 
Maintenance Fund to the Operating Requirement and (ii) promptly deposit all of the remaining 
Revenues to the credit of the Revenue Fund with the Trustee or in the name of the Trustee with a 
depositary or depositaries, each fully qualified under the Indenture to receive the same as deposits 
of money held by the Trustee, designated by the City and approved by the Trustee. 
The moneys in the Revenue Fund shall be disbursed and applied by the Trustee as required 
to make the following deposits and payments on the dates and in the amounts provided: 
On the last business day of the month immediately preceding each January 1 and 
July 1, the Trustee shall make the following deposits and payments in the manner and order 
of priority set forth: 
FIRST, the Trustee shall first deposit into the Debt Service Fund the amount 
necessary to increase the amount on deposit therein to an amount sufficient to fund the 
Deposit Requirements corresponding to that January 1 or July 1, which amount (when 
added to the amounts then held in the applicable Dedicated Sub-Funds) shall be at least 
equal to the sum of (i) the aggregate Senior Lien Debt Service to be paid during the 
Applicable Payment Period, plus (ii) the aggregate amount of Principal Installments of and 
interest on Senior Lien Section 208 Obligations to be paid during the Applicable Payment 
Period, plus (iii) the amount, if any, required to cause the amount on deposit in the Common 
Debt Service Reserve Sub-Fund to be equal to the amount then required, plus (iv) the 
amount, if any, required to cause the amount on deposit in each debt service reserve account 
(other than the Common Debt Service Reserve Sub-Fund) established for any Senior Lien 
Obligation to be equal to the amount then required to be held in such account as provided 
in the Supplemental Indenture or the instrument creating such Senior Lien Obligation. 
SECOND, the Trustee shall next deposit into the Junior Lien Obligation Debt 
Service Fund an amount, if any, equal to the aggregate amounts required for the next semi-
annual period by any indenture, agreement or ordinance authorizing the issuance of Junior 
Lien Obligations to be deposited therein on such date and except as otherwise directed by 
the City, without priority, one over the other, to any sub-funds or accounts within the Junior 
Lien Obligation Debt Service Fund, the amount or amounts specified by one or more 
Certificates of the City filed with the Trustee.  
3 
 
THIRD, the Trustee shall next deposit into the Renewal and Replacement Fund the 
lesser of (i) the amount equal to twenty-five percent (25%) of the then current System 
Reserve Requirement and (ii) the amount, if any, required to increase the amount in the 
Renewal and Replacement Fund to the then current System Reserve Requirement. 
FOURTH, at the direction of the City expressed in a Certificate of the City filed 
with the Trustee, the Trustee shall next pay to each Swap Provider under a Qualified Senior 
Lien Swap Agreement, the amount specified in such Certificate to be paid in respect of a 
Termination Payment payable to such Swap Provider. 
FIFTH, the Trustee shall next transfer to the City for deposit into the System 
General Fund any amount remaining in the Revenue Fund unless the City shall have filed 
with the Trustee a Certificate specifying a lesser amount, in which case the amount 
specified by the City in the Certificate shall be the amount to be transferred to the City at 
such time for deposit into the System General Fund. 
If at the time deposits are required to be made the moneys held in the Revenue Fund are 
insufficient to make any required deposit, the deposit shall be made up on the next applicable 
deposit date after required deposits into all other Funds enjoying a higher priority shall have been 
made in full. 
Amounts on deposit in the Debt Service Fund, the Junior Lien Obligation Debt Service 
Fund and the Renewal and Replacement Fund in excess of the amount required hereunder or under 
any Supplemental Indenture or under any indenture, agreement or ordinance authorizing the 
issuance of Junior Lien Obligations to be on deposit in such Fund at the end of such Fiscal Year 
shall be transferred to the Revenue Fund. 
THE BONDS 
General 
The Bonds will bear interest at the rates per annum and mature in the amounts and on the 
dates set forth on the inside cover page of this Official Statement. Principal of and interest on the 
Bonds will be paid as described in APPENDIX C – BOOK-ENTRY ONLY SYSTEM hereto. 
The Bonds are issuable only as fully registered bonds in denominations of $5,000 and any integral 
multiples thereof. The Bonds will bear interest (based on a 360-day year of twelve 30-day months) 
from their date and will be payable semiannually on January 1 and July 1 of each year, 
commencing July 1, 2026. The Bonds, as initially issued, will be dated as of the date of delivery. 
The principal of the Bonds shall be payable in lawful money of the United States of 
America upon presentation and surrender thereof at the corporate trust office of U.S. Bank Trust 
Company, National Association, Chicago, Illinois, which has been appointed as Trustee under the 
Master Trust Indenture and as the Paying Agent for the Bonds. Interest on the Bonds shall be 
payable on each interest payment date to the registered owners of record thereof appearing on the 
registration books maintained by the City for such purpose at the corporate trust office of the 
Trustee, as of the close of business on the 15 th day of the calendar month next preceding the 
applicable interest payment date. The Bonds will be issued initially in book-entry only form. See 
APPENDIX C - BOOK-ENTRY ONLY SYSTEM hereto.  
4 
 
Redemption Prior to Maturity 
Optional Redemption .  The Bonds maturing on or after January 1, 2036 are subject to  
redemption, at the option of the City, on or after January 1, 2035, as a whole or in part at any time 
and if in part, in such principal amounts and from such maturities as the City shall determine and 
by lot for Bonds of the same maturity, at a redemption price equal to the principal amount thereof 
to be redeemed plus accrued interest to the date of redemption.  
Mandatory Sinking Fund Redemption.  The Bonds maturing on January 1, 2050 are subject 
to mandatory redemption, in part and by lot at a redemption price of par on January 1 of the years 
and in the principal amounts as follows: 
Bonds due January 1, 2050 
Year Principal Amount 
2046 $7,615,000 
2047 8,020,000 
2048 8,440,000 
2049 8,885,000 
2050 (stated maturity) 9,350,000 
The principal amounts of Bonds to be mandatorily redeemed in each year may be reduced 
through the earlier optional redemption thereof, with any partial optional redemption of such 
Bonds credited against future mandatory sinking fund payments on the final maturity amount as 
the City may determine and in the absence of such determination, shall be created against the 
unsatisfied balance of the applicable sinking fund payment next ensuing. In addition, on or prior 
to the 60th day preceding any mandatory redemption date the Trustee may, and if directed by the 
City shall, apply the moneys held from the payment of the applicable sinking fund payment to 
purchase Bonds required to be retired on such mandatory redemption date. The purchase price paid 
for such Bond (excluding accrued interest) shall not exceed par. Any such Bonds so purchased 
shall be cancelled and the principal amount thereof shall be credited against the mandatory 
redemption required on such next mandatory redemption date. 
Partial Redemption .  In the event of the redemption of less than all the Bonds of like 
maturity, the aggregate principal amount thereof to be redeemed shall be $5,000 or an integral 
multiple thereof and the Trustee shall select by lot the Bonds to be redeemed. Whenever the Bonds 
are held in book-entry form, the Bonds to be redeemed shall be selected by DTC in accordance 
with its applicable procedures. 
Notice of Redemption.  Notice of the redemption of Bonds or any portion thereof 
identifying the Bonds or portions thereof to be redeemed, specifying the redemption date, the 
Redemption Price, the places and dates of payment, that from the redemption date interest will 
cease to accrue, and, in the case of any optional redemption, whether the redemption is conditioned 
upon sufficient moneys being available on the redemption date (or any other condition), shall be 
given by the Trustee by mailing a copy of such redemption notice not less than 30 nor more than 
60 days prior to the date fixed for redemption, to the Registered Owner of each Bond to be 
redeemed in whole or in part at the address shown on the registration books. Redemption notices  
5 
 
shall be sent by first class mail, except that notices to Registered Owners of at least $1,000,000 of 
Bonds shall be sent by registered mail. Failure to mail any such notice to the Registered Owner of 
any Bond or any defect therein shall not affect the validity of the proceedings for such redemption 
of Bonds. Whenever the Bonds are held in book-entry form, redemption notices will be delivered 
in accordance with the applicable procedures of the DTC, which may include electronic delivery. 
Any notice given shall be conclusively presumed to have been duly given, whether or not the 
Registered Owner of any Bond receives the notice.

PLAN OF FINANCE 
The City is issuing the Bonds for the purpose of (i) financing a portion of the costs of the 
Water Transmission System Project (ii) making a deposit to the Common Debt Service Reserve 
Sub-Fund and (iii) paying costs of issuance of the Bonds. 
THE WATER TRANSMISSION SYSTEM PROJECT 
 
 
 
7 
 
The City’s current primary water source is a deep sandstone aquifer, which, due to unique 
geological features, allows for limited natural recharge of the aquifer through the ground. 
Furthermore, migration of water to the City is impeded by the Sandwich Fault. For many years, 
water withdrawals have exceeded the sustainable yield of the aquifer. In 2015, the Illinois State 
Water Survey ("ISWS") published results of groundwater modeling indicating desaturation of the 
aquifer providing water to the City could occur within 15-30 years. Further groundwater modeling 
completed by ISWS in 2018 and updated in 2020 found that at current usage rates, the City’s 
existing water source may not meet maximum day demands by 2030.  In 2020, the ISWS published 
a report showing increased concentrations of chlorides and total dissolved solids in wells from the 
shallow aquifer. Also in 2020, sampling by the IEPA of water from shallow aquifer wells have 
detectible levels of PFAS at or above levels now regulated by the USEPA. 
Water Transmission System Project 
To address this impending water shortage, the City embarked on a multi-year study to 
explore alternative water sources. From August 2018 to January 2019, the City evaluated 14 water 
source alternatives, assessing each option’s quality and quantity of water that would be available. 
At the conclusion of this portion of the study, five of the alternatives that met the water quality and 
quantity criteria were further evaluated across additional metrics such as governance, risk, 
operation and maintenance, and cost. Based on this evaluation,  in January 2020, the Joliet City 
Council selected Lake Michigan as the alternative water source for the City and directed staff to 
further evaluate two alternatives: (1) purchasing treated Lake Michigan water from the City of 
Chicago and (2) drawing raw Lake Michigan water via an intake in Indiana and transmitting it to 
Joliet for treatment. In January 2021, the City formally selected the City of Chicago as its preferred 
partner for an alternative water source and entered into a Preliminary Agreement with respect to 
an Anticipated Water Supply Agreement with the City of Chicago. Later in 2021, the City and 
other municipalities in the region adopted resolutions declaring their intent to negotiate creation 
of a new water commission to provide Lake Michigan water. 
The City has completed preliminary engineering design of the Water Transmission System 
Project and is currently in the final engineering design phase. Construction began in 2025 and will 
run through 2030, at which point the City will begin providing Lake Michigan water to its 
customers. 
The cost of purchased water includes various rate caps and is based on a cost-of-service 
methodology that will allow for the City to only pay for facilities and their associated operating 
and maintenance costs which are required to supply water to the City. 
The City’s expected benefits from the Water Transmission System Project include: 
 High quality water source from Lake Michigan that will eliminate the need for water 
softeners and purchase of bottled water by City residents. 
 Collaboration with the City of Chicago to provide finished water to the City and the 
broader region via an established water supply that has provided water to millions of 
customers in northeastern Illinois for over 100 years.   
8 
 
 Sustainable water quantity to serve the City and its regional partners presently and in 
the future.  
 Ability to complete improvements and bring new water source online by 2030. 
 A guaranteed fair and equitable purchased water cost based on an established American 
Water Works Association cost of service methodology for which the City only pays for 
the cost to construct, operate and maintain facilities used to provide water to the City.  
 Opportunity to have input on City of Chicago water service to the City and rate setting 
via an Advisory Council established by Chicago consisting of representatives of its 
wholesale customers.  
Chicago Water Supply Agreement 
On May 1, 2023, the City finalized a 100-year Water Supply Agreement with the City of 
Chicago ("Chicago") to purchase treated Lake Michigan water beginning in 2030 ("Chicago Water 
Supply Agreement"). Pursuant to this Agreement, Chicago has agreed to provide a supply of 
treated Lake Michigan Water through December 31, 2123 in an amount up to 105 million gallons 
per day. This quantity was negotiated to be sufficient to provide the estimated demand for water 
required by the member municipalities of the Grand Prairie Water Commission (described in more 
detail below under the heading "Grand Prairie Water Commission") at their anticipated full 
community buildout.   
Lake Michigan Water treated by the City of Chicago is sold by Chicago to more than 120 
wholesale customers and serves more than 5.3 million customers in the metropolitan Chicago 
region. Chicago treats Lake Michigan Water through two water filtration plants. Water provided 
under the Chicago Water Supply Agreement will be treated at the Eugene Sawyer Water 
Purification Plant. When delivery of water begins under the Chicago Water Supply Agreement, 
the volume provided to the City will make the City one of Chicago’s five largest wholesale water 
customers. 
The Chicago Water Supply Agreement represents a change in Chicago’s method of 
charging for wholesale water supply from its flat rate system. This Agreement establishes water 
rates through a cost-of-service methodology that charges customers based on their proportionate 
share of the cost of providing water service. The Chicago Water Supply Agreement provides 
substantial detail about the elements of the Chicago water system that are included in the cost-of-
service methodology, and specifically excludes costs attributable to items such as replacement of 
lead service lines for Chicago retail customers, installation of new water meters for Chicago retail 
customers, and various other costs not associated with the provision of water service to wholesale 
customers. 
As part of the establishment of the Commission, the City assigned the Chicago Water 
Supply Agreement with the City of Chicago to the Commission. The assignment to the 
Commission was completed on August 13, 2025.  
9 
 
Grand Prairie Water Commission 
The City is leading efforts to develop and design the Water Transmission System Project. 
These efforts have included working with multiple nearby municipalities to form a regional water 
commission. In June 2024, six municipalities (Village of Channahon, City of Crest Hill, City of 
Joliet, Village of Minooka, Village of Romeoville and Village of Shorewood) each passed an 
ordinance and entered into an intergovernmental agreement to establish a regional water 
commission known as the Grand Prairie Water Commission (the "Commission"). The creation of 
the Commission was enabled by the passage of legislation by the State of Illinois, which was 
signed into law by Governor Pritzker on December 16, 2021 as 65 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/11-
135.5-1 et seq., and amended by Public Act 102-1134, effective February 1, 2023. This legislation 
establishes the Regional Water Commissions Act, which allows municipalities to form a regional 
commission to acquire a common source of water supply and build, own, and operate a water 
system. To be a part of a regional water commission, municipalities must include at least one 
municipality with at least 140,000 inhabitants that is located in Cook, Kane, Kendall, Lake, 
McHenry, or Will counties. The City meets this population threshold and location requirement. 
The Commission is an independent governmental entity that is separate from each member and 
was formed as of June 28, 2024. 
As part of the establishment of the Commission, two other key agreements were approved: 
the six municipalities joining the Commission approved a master Water Supply Agreement among 
the six municipalities and the Commission dated July 2, 2024 ("Commission Water Supply 
Agreement"), and the Commission and the City entered into an Intergovernmental Agreement for 
Program Management dated July 2, 2024 ("Program Management Agreement"). 
The Commission will construct, own and maintain all of the common transmission mains 
and water facilities upstream of each member community metering point. The construction portion 
of the Water Transmission System Project that is being funded by the Commission is expected to 
cost approximately $1.188 billion. Future borrowings for the construction portion of the Water 
Transmission System Project are expected to be undertaken by the Commission. The Commission 
is in the process of finalizing its Master Indenture that is expected to secure future indebtedness 
incurred by the Commission. The Commission is currently in negotiations with the USEPA on the 
terms of an initial WIFIA Loan that will finance a portion of its costs associated with the Water 
Transmission System Project. The Commission expects to also enter into IEPA Loans in the future, 
in addition to issuing Commission Revenue Bonds. The Commission issued $51,200,000 Senior 
Lien Water Revenue Bonds, Series 2025, which is expected to close on November 13, 2025. 
Program Management Agreement 
The Commission and the City have entered into the Program Management Agreement, 
pursuant to which the City will provide both Program Management Services and Commission 
Management Services for the Commission. Program Management Services includes managing 
both the design and construction of the Water Transmission System Project that will be 
constructed, owned and maintained by the Commission. Commission Management Services 
include services that would typically be performed by Commission employees. However, as of the 
date of issuance of the Bonds, the Commission has no employees.    
10 
 
The Program Management Agreement establishes a fixed Management Services fee to be 
paid by the Commission to the City. This fee will be included as part of the City’s Advanced 
Development Costs and Advanced Construction Costs, as discussed in the section on "Commission 
Water Supply Agreement" below. 
Commission Water Supply Agreement 
The Commission Water Supply Agreement provides that the Commission is obligated to 
sell Lake Michigan Water to the members and each member is obligated to purchase all water 
necessary to meet its full water requirements. Upon assignment of the Chicago Water Supply 
Agreement to the Commission (discussed under "Chicago Water Supply Agreement" above), the 
Commission will have the necessary water supply to serve the members. Each member has 
obtained a Lake Michigan water allocation permit from the State of Illinois pursuant to which the 
member has the right to obtain Lake Michigan water, and the members are required to maintain in 
effect a permit for a sufficient allocation of Lake Michigan water to meet its requested amount of 
water. Each member has declared the quantity of its anticipated water demand through the year 
2050 and an estimated water demand for the member at its full community buildout.  
Commission members are required to make payments, on a "take or pay" basis, under the 
Commission Water Supply Agreement based on formulas provided for various categories of costs, 
including purchased water costs (including costs paid to Chicago), capital and debt service costs 
(including costs of financing), operation and maintenance costs, reserve maintenance costs, 
general administrative costs, and default costs (if any). Payments to the Commission from the 
members, including payments for Commission debt service, are operation and maintenance 
expenses of the member’s municipal system and are not a debt of any member, and are to be paid 
to the Commission prior to any payment on the Bonds. Therefore, the City will be required to 
make these payments to the Commission prior to making payments on the Bonds. 
The City has advanced and incurred costs in connection with development of an alternative 
water source program, the design and development of the Water System Transmission Project and 
the development of the Commission for the period commencing in February 2021 and will 
continue to advance and incur these costs ("Advanced Development Costs") as well as costs for 
pre-construction and construction services in connection with the Water System Transmission 
Project ("Advanced Construction Costs"). The Commission Water Supply Agreement provides 
that the City shall receive a credit toward amounts it will owe for its share of capital costs, debt 
service and costs of financing in the amount of the Advanced Development Costs and Advanced 
Construction Costs that it incurs. The Bonds are solely an obligation of the City payable from the 
Revenues as defined in the Master Indenture, and the City will continue to borrow for the 
Advanced Development Costs and Advanced Construction Costs pursuant to the Commission 
Water Supply Agreement. 
The City’s allocation of Commission capital costs, debt service and costs of financing is 
based on the City’s declared share of maximum day demand for the Commission system as of 
2050, which is approximately 58%. The City will receive a credit toward its future share of 
Commission capital costs, debt service and costs of financing for the Advanced Development 
Costs and Advanced Construction Costs, which is anticipated to result in the City’s adjusted share 
of the Commission capital costs, debt service and costs of financing  being approximately 49%.  
11 
 
Each member will construct, own, operate and maintain its own watermains and water 
facilities downstream of its metering point(s) at the point of connection with Commission 
transmissions mains.   
Water Main Replacement Project 
The City is currently engaged in a Water Main Replacement Project aimed at reducing 
leakage throughout the System prior to the date on which the City would begin to purchase Lake 
Michigan Water as required by the City’s Lake Michigan water allocation permit. This includes 
the replacement of all water mains constructed prior to the 1970s. The total cost of the Water Main 
Replacement Project is estimated at $623 million. Proceeds of the Bonds are not anticipated to 
fund any portion of the costs of the Water Main Replacement Project. However, the City does 
intend to use a variety of sources of funding for future costs related to the Water Main Replacement 
Project including Revenue Bonds. 
Estimated Project Costs and Funding Sources – The City 
The City currently expects to use a variety of funding sources for the financing of both the 
Water Transmission System Project and the Water Main Replacement Project. This may include 
the use of Senior Lien Obligations or Junior Lien Obligations including Revenue Bonds, Illinois 
Environmental Protection Act ("IEPA") Loans and WIFIA Loans.

Impact on Water and Sewer Rates 
The City expects to enact future increases in water and sewer rates in order to ensure timely 
payment of principal and interest on any Senior Lien Obligations, including WIFIA Loans, and 
Junior Lien Obligations, including IEPA Loans, issued to fund the Project. These increases are 
subject to City Council approval and are expected to be considered in three-year increments by 
City Council. The City will be responsible for setting rates in a manner that will ensure it will 
make timely payments on its own Water System indebtedness, as well as satisfy its obligations to 
make payments to the Commission for the purchase of its share of treated water. The purchase of 
treated water from the Commission will be an Operating Expense of the City’s Water System. The 
City has agreed to purchase a minimum volume of water from the Commission as part of its Water 
Supply Agreement.

SECURITY FOR THE BONDS 
The Bonds shall be limited obligations of the City payable from the Revenues (as defined 
in the Master Indenture) of the System and certain other moneys and securities held by the Trustee 
under the Master Indenture and the Second Supplemental Indenture. The Bonds shall not constitute 
an indebtedness or a loan of the credit of the City within the meaning of any constitutional or 
statutory limitation and neither the full faith and credit nor the taxing power of the City is pledged 
to the payment of the principal of or the interest on the Bonds. 
Pursuant to the Master Indenture the Bonds shall be payable from, and secured by a pledge 
of, lien on and security interest in the Trust Estate consisting of (i) the Revenues, (ii) amounts on 
deposit in the Funds, Accounts and Dedicated Sub-Funds established under the Master Indenture 
and the Second Supplemental Indenture creating the Bonds and (iii) all other moneys held from 
time to time under the Master Indenture and the Second Supplemental Indenture for the payment 
of the Bonds. The WIFIA Loans and additional Bonds are also Senior Lien Obligations. 
Please see APPENDIX E – SUMMARY OF CERTAIN PROVISIONS OF THE 
INDENTURE for more detail on the sub-sections below. 
Common Debt Service Reserve Sub-Fund 
Furthermore, the Bonds will be secured by the Common Debt Service Reserve Sub-Fund.  
The Common Debt Service Reserve Sub-Fund will be funded at the Reserve Requirement, which 
is equal to Maximum Annual Debt Service for all outstanding debt service at the time of issuance 
of any new Senior Lien indebtedness. This includes both the Revenue Bonds and the WIFIA 
Loans. The Reserve Requirement may be satisfied with (i) one or more Qualified Credit 
Instruments, (ii) Qualified Investments, or (iii) a combination thereof.   
The moneys in the Common Debt Service Reserve Sub-Fund are held for the benefit of all 
Common Reserve Bonds and are pledged and assigned for that purpose. On the date of initial 
issuance of any Series of Senior Lien Obligations intended to be Common Reserve Bonds, the City 
shall provide the Trustee a Certificate to that effect and setting forth the amount of the deposit to 
be made from proceeds of such Series to fund the Reserve Requirement. The City will determine 
at the time of issuance of any future Series of Senior Lien Obligations if they will be designated 
as Common Reserve Bonds. 
Rate and Coverage Covenant 
Pursuant to the Indenture, the City covenants that it will fix and establish, and revise from 
time to time whenever necessary, the Service Charges for the use and operation of the System and 
for services rendered by the City in the operation of the System in order that Revenues in each 
Fiscal Year, together with Other Available Moneys deposited with the Trustee with respect to that 
Fiscal Year will be at least sufficient: (i) to provide for the payment of Operating Expenses for the 
Fiscal Year; and (ii) to provide for the greater of (A) the sum of (1) the amounts needed to make 
the deposits (exclusive of deposits to the System General Fund) required to be made pursuant to 
the Indenture and all other ordinances, indentures and agreements pursuant to which all 
Outstanding Senior Lien Obligations or other outstanding System Obligations are issued and 
secured, and (2) any additional amounts needed to provide for any deficits resulting from failure  
14 
 
to receive any Service Charges and to pay and discharge all charges or liens payable out of 
Revenues when due and enforceable, and (B) for each Fiscal Year, one and fifteen-hundredths 
times Aggregate Debt Service for the Applicable Bond Year, such Aggregate Debt Service to be 
reduced by any proceeds of System Obligations held by the Trustee for disbursement during that 
Bond Year to pay principal of and interest of Senior Lien Obligations. If during any Fiscal Year, 
Revenues and Other Available Moneys to be deposited with the Trustee are estimated to produce 
less than the amount required, the City shall revise its schedule of Service Charges or alter its 
methods of operation or take other action in such manner as is necessary to produce the amount so 
required in such Fiscal Year. 
Additional Bonds Test Under the Master Indenture 
Prior to the issuance of any Senior Lien Obligations, the City will receive either (A) a 
Certificate of an Independent Accountant or a Certificate of the City, in either case stating that the 
sum of Net Revenues and Other Available Moneys in the most recent completed Fiscal Year 
ending within the last 24 months for which audited financial statements have been prepared was 
not less than one hundred fifteen percent (115%) of Maximum Annual Debt Service as of the time 
immediately after the issuance of the Series of Senior Lien Obligations proposed to be issued or 
(B) a Certificate of the Independent System Consultant (1) projecting the sum of Net Revenues 
and Other Available Moneys for each of the five Fiscal Years next following the date of issuance 
of the Series of Senior Lien Obligations proposed to be issued; (2) setting forth the Maximum 
Annual Debt Service as of the time immediately following the issuance of such Series and (3) 
determining that the sum of such Net Revenues and Other Available Moneys for each of such five 
Fiscal Years will not be less than one hundred fifteen percent (115%) of such Maximum Annual 
Debt Service. 
A Certificate representing compliance with part (A) of the Additional Bonds Test in the 
paragraph above is included in APPENDIX F - COVERAGE REPORT OF RATE 
CONSULTANT, the form of which includes debt service of the Bonds and the estimated 
repayment schedule for the two WIFIA Loans that were approved by City Council on March 15, 
2022 and the WIFIA Loan approved by the City Council on August 19, 2025. The Master Trust 
Indenture allows for Net Revenues and Other Available Moneys of the most recent completed 
Fiscal Year for use in the Certificate to be adjusted to account for any adjustments to Service 
Charges that have been approved by the City Council. The Certificate incorporates adjustments to 
Fiscal Year 2024 Net Revenues Available for Debt Service by applying increases to Service 
Charges that have previously been approved by City Council for 2026 and 2027. 
THE WATERWORKS AND SEWERAGE SYSTEM 
The System of the City is comprised of the waterworks and sanitary sewerage utilities 
described below. 
Water System 
The City’s current water supply is obtained from 21 deep wells and five shallow wells. 
Water is pumped from the ground, treated at the City’s 11 water treatment plants and chlorinated 
before being pumped either into storage or to the distribution system. A blended polyphosphate is  
15 
 
also added as a corrosion inhibitor. System storage includes 12 million gallons of ground reservoirs 
and 4.5 million gallons of elevated storage. The existing water distribution system consists of 679 
miles of water main including 9,137 fire hydrants. 
Water system demand varies from a minimum of 11.46 million gallons per day ("mgd") to 
a maximum of 17.86 mgd. Existing capacity of the System is 34.5 mgd which, when combined 
with storage, is more than adequate for peak requirements. 
Sanitary Sewerage System  
The City operates three wastewater treatment plants. The Eastside Wastewater Treatment 
Plant is rated to treat an average flow of 18.2 mgd and a peak flow of 45.5 mgd. The sewers 
connected to the Eastside Wastewater Treatment Plant are a combination of sanitary sewers and 
combined sewers. This plant serves the eastern half of the City. In addition, this plant provides 
regional treatment services for the East Joliet Sanitary District, the Southeast Joliet Sanitary 
District, and the Village of Rockdale. In 2018, wet weather treatment facilities were constructed 
at this facility capable of treating 90 mgd of flow from the combined sewer systems reducing the 
potential for combined sewer overflows to the Des Plaines River as required by the City’s approved 
Long Term Control Plan. In 2020, the facility was upgraded to provide for the removal of 
phosphorus. This plant treated an average flow of 17.09 mgd in 2024. 
The Westside Wastewater Treatment Plant was placed in service in 1976. Plant upgrades 
were completed in 2003 and 2019. After the upgrades, the plant is rated to treat 14 mgd average 
flow for the removal of BOD (Biochemical Oxygen Demand), suspended solids, ammonia 
nitrogen and phosphorus. The maximum flow rate for the plant is 28 mgd. The average flow for 
the plant in 2024 was 10.28 mgd. During the 2003 upgrades, a stormwater pumping station and 
stormwater storage basin were constructed to address large wet weather flows in the collection 
system tributary to the Joliet Westside Wastewater Treatment Plant. The stormwater pumping 
station delivers a portion of the flow received at the treatment plant into the stormwater basin. This 
flow is stored until the influent decreases below 28 mgd. At that time, the flows are returned to the 
plant for treatment. The entire area serviced by the Westside Wastewater Treatment Plant is 
serviced by separate sanitary sewers. The Westside Wastewater Treatment Plant provides 
treatment for two-thirds of the western half of the City. In addition, this plant provides regional 
treatment services for the Sunnyland Sanitary District, the eastern portion of the Village of 
Channahon, and the Village of Shorewood. 
The Aux Sable Creek Basin Wastewater Treatment Plant was placed into service in 2006. 
A plant expansion was completed in 2019. The plant is serviced by separate sanitary sewers and 
the plant provides treatment for the western one-third of the City. The plant is rated to treat 7.7 
mgd average day flow and a peak flow of 17.3 mgd for the removal of BOD, suspended solids, 
ammonia nitrogen and phosphorus. The average flow for the plant in 2024 was 4.68 mgd. 
The wastewater collection system consists of 602 miles of combined and separate sanitary 
sewers.

Billing and Collecting 
Bills are sent out monthly and are due and payable within 15 days and considered to be 
delinquent thereafter. An interest charge of 1.5 percent per month of the outstanding balance is 
charged after 15 days. If payment is not received within 60 days, the customer is notified that 
service will be discontinued within an additional 15 days. 
Unpaid charges become a lien on the real estate for which service has been provided within 
90 days. 
Connections Required 
The Joliet Municipal Code requires connection to the water distribution and sanitary sewer 
system when mains are accessible. All newly annexed properties within a certain distance of a 
public water main must connect to the City System upon annexation. Properties already in the City 
with operating wells are allowed to continue using those wells. All premises connected to the City 
water supply must have water meters.

SYSTEM DEBT INFORMATION 
After issuance of the Bonds, the City will have $214,819,933 of Senior Lien Obligations 
outstanding. The City also has $243,599,392 of IEPA Loans outstanding at the time of issuance 
and $52,331,184 of IEPA Loans which remain available to draw down which share a junior lien 
of the Revenues of the System. The City entered into the WIFIA Loans in the amount of 
$308,454,947 on April 19, 2022 that are also Senior Lien Obligations. As of the issuance of the 
Bonds, $102,599,933 has been drawn on the WIFIA Loans. The City is also working with the 
USEPA on the issuance of a third WIFIA Loan in the amount of $86,926,000 for the funding of a 
portion of the Water Transmission System Project. The City has also been awarded $139,929,542 
from the Illinois EPA in an additional IEPA Loan for the Water Main Replacement Project.

WIFIA Re-Amortization 
On April 19, 2022, the City closed on two WIFIA Loans for a total available amount of 
$308,454,947. At closing, an original amortization schedule was established for each WIFIA Loan. 
The City is working with the USEPA to amend the amortization schedules for each loan in order 
to better accommodate the upcoming debt service requirements of the City’s upcoming 
borrowings. 
Based on the current draws on WIFIA Loans of $102,599,933, at the time of closing of the 
Bonds, the maximum annual debt service on Senior Lien Obligations is estimated to be 
$18,775,521. After the expected re-amortization of the WIFIA Loans, the maximum annual debt 
service on Senior Lien Obligations is estimated to be $18,343,620. The City expects to finalize the 
re-amortization of the WIFIA Loans in 2026. 
SYSTEM FINANCIAL INFORMATION 
Basis of Accounting 
The financial statements for the Waterworks and Sewerage System reflect the accrual basis 
method of accounting. Revenues are recognized in the accounting period in which they are earned 
and become measurable; expenses are recognized when incurred. Utility services provided, but 
not yet billed, are estimated and recorded as revenue in the period that service is provided. 
In recent years, the City has capitalized acquisitions of property and equipment of the 
Waterworks and Sewerage System. However, the System’s property and equipment is not 
presented in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles in the financial statements 
because a material portion of the property and equipment recorded in the Waterworks and 
Sewerage Fund is from an era where inventory records are not readily attainable or comparable.   
The following tables are summaries, excerpted from the audited financial statements of the 
City, copies of which are available upon request. Please see APPENDIX A - AUDIT REPORT 
FOR FISCAL YEAR ENDED DECEMBER 31, 2024 for excerpts from the City’s 2024 audited

THE CITY 
The City derived its name from the French-Canadian explorer, Louis Joliet, who visited 
the area in 1673. 
"Juliet" was incorporated by an act of Legislature as a village in the year 1837, and was 
governed by a President and Board of Trustees until 1841, when by an act of the State Legislature 
the village charter was repealed and the trustees resigned, leaving Juliet without an organization 
until June 19, 1852, at which time the City was incorporated by an act of the State Legislature.  
The act of incorporation was approved by the electors on July 5, 1852 by a vote of 168 for, 133 
against. 
In the year 1857, a new charter for the City was passed by the State Legislature, which 
remained in force (with some minor amendments) until August 5, 1876, at which time by a vote 
of the City the general Act to provide for the incorporation of cities and villages, approved on 
April 10, 1872, and in force on July 1, 1872, was adopted by a vote of 1,076 for, 307 against. 
The City encompasses approximately 63 square miles and is the County seat of Will 
County in the Des Plaines River Valley, 39 miles southwest of Chicago. Census population reports 
have been: 1970 – 78,827; 1980 – 77,956; 1990 – 76,836; 2000 – 106,221; 2010 – 147,433 and 
2020 – 150,362. 
As a home rule City under the 1970 Illinois Constitution, the City has no general obligation 
debt limit. In addition, it is not required to seek referendum approval for the issuance of bonds and 
has no statutory tax rate limitations for any purpose. 
Government 
The City operates under a council manager form of government with five council persons 
elected from districts, a Mayor, and three council persons elected at-large, and an appointed City 
Manager. In the capacity of administrative head of the City, the Manager supervises the 
performance of approximately 1,032 full and part-time municipal employees. The Joliet Municipal 
Building (150 W. Jefferson, Joliet, Illinois, 60432) houses the administrative offices of the City.  
The City has a class III fire insurance rating, among the best ratings in the State. The City provides 
trash removal and disposal and recycling services through a private contractor. The City operates 
a water supply and distribution system and sanitary sewer system (see "THE WATERWORKS AND 
SEWERAGE SYSTEM").

RISK FACTORS 
The purchase of the Bonds involves certain investment risks. Accordingly, each 
prospective purchaser of the Bonds should make an independent evaluation of the entirety of the 
information presented in this Official Statement and its appendices and exhibits in order to make 
an informed investment decision. Certain of the investment risks are described below. The 
following statements, however, should not be considered a complete description of all risks to be 
considered in the decision to purchaser the Bonds, nor should the order of the presentation of such 
risks be construed to reflect the relative importance of the various risks. There can be no assurance 
that other risk factors are not material or will not become material in the future. Moreover, any one 
or more of the factors discussed under this heading, and other factors not described under this 
heading, could lead to a decrease in the market value and the liquidity of the Bonds. 
Finances of the State of Illinois 
The State of Illinois (the "State") has experienced adverse fiscal conditions resulting in 
significant shortfalls between the State's general fund revenues and spending demands. 
Underfunding of the State's pension systems has contributed to the State's poor financial health. 
The State's financial problems may affect the strength of the local economy.  
Local Economy 
The financial health of the City is in part dependent on the strength of the regional and state 
economy. Many factors affect the economy, including rates of employment and economic growth 
and the level of residential and commercial development. It is not possible to predict to what extent 
any changes in economic conditions, demographic characteristics, population, or commercial and 
industrial activity will occur and what impact such changes would have on the finances of the City. 
Cybersecurity 
Computer networks and data transmission and collection are vital to the efficient operation 
of the City. Despite the implementation of network security measures by the City, its information 
technology and infrastructure may be vulnerable to deliberate attacks by hackers, malware, 
ransomware, or computer virus, or may otherwise be breached due to employee error, malfeasance, 
or other disruptions. Any such breach could compromise networks, and the information stored 
thereon could be disrupted, accessed, publicly disclosed, lost, or stolen. Although the City does 
not believe that its information technology systems are at a materially greater risk of cybersecurity 
attacks than other similarly-situated governmental entities, any such disruption, access, disclosure, 
or other loss of information could have an adverse effect on the City's operations and financial 
health. Further, as cybersecurity threats continue to evolve, the City may be required to expend 
significant additional resources to continue to modify and strengthen security measures, 
investigate, and remediate any vulnerabilities, or invest in new technology designed to mitigate 
security risks.  
33 
 
Construction and Inflation Risks 
There are potential risks that could affect the ability of the City to timely complete the 
Project. While preliminary costs have been projected by the City, not all of the construction 
contracts have been let by the City. No assurance can be given that the cost of completing the 
Project will not exceed available funds. Completion of the Project involves many risks common 
to construction projects such as shortages or delays in the availability of materials and labor, work 
stoppages, labor disputes, contractual disputes with contractors or suppliers, weather interferences, 
construction accidents, delays in obtaining legal approvals, unforeseen engineering, archeological 
or environmental problems, inflationary pressures and other unanticipated cost increases, any of 
which could give rise to significant delays or cost overruns. 
Future Indebtedness 
As described under "Estimated Project Costs and Funding Sources – The City," the City 
expects that it will need to incur additional indebtedness, including the issuance of Revenue Bonds, 
WIFIA Loans, and IEPA Loans, to finance the Water Transmission System Project. No assurance 
can be given that these sources of funding actually will be available in the amounts or on the 
schedules assumed. In addition to the Water Transmission System Project, the City may, from time 
to time, determine to fund additional System capital projects including the Water Main 
Replacement Project. 
Loss or Change of Rating 
The ratings assigned to the Bonds can be changed or withdrawn at any time for reasons 
both under and outside the City's control. Any change, withdrawal or combination thereof could 
adversely affect the ability of investors to sell the Bonds or may affect the price at which they can 
be sold. 
Secondary Market for the Bonds 
No assurance can be given that a secondary market will develop for the purchase and sale 
of the Bonds or, if a secondary market exists, that such Bonds can be sold for any particular price. 
The Underwriters are not obligated to engage in secondary market trading or to repurchase any of 
the Bonds at the request of the owners thereof. 
Prices of the Bonds as traded in the secondary market are subject to adjustment upward 
and downward in response to changes in the credit markets and other prevailing circumstances.  
No guarantee exists as to the future market value of the Bonds. Such market value could be 
substantially different from the original purchase price. 
Continuing Disclosure 
A failure by the City to comply with the Undertaking (as defined herein) for continuing 
disclosure (see "CONTINUING DISCLOSURE" herein) will not constitute an event of default on the 
Bonds. Any such failure must be reported in accordance with Rule 15c2-12 (the "Rule") adopted 
by the Securities and Exchange Commission under the Securities Exchange Act of 1934, as  
34 
 
amended (the "Exchange Act"), and may adversely affect the transferability and liquidity of the 
Bonds and their market price. 
Suitability of Investment 
The interest rates borne by the Bonds are intended to compensate the investor for assuming 
the risk of investing in the Bonds. Furthermore, the tax-exempt feature of the Bonds is currently 
more valuable to high tax bracket investors than to investors that are in low tax brackets. As such, 
the value of the interest compensation to any particular investor will vary with individual tax rates 
and circumstances. Each prospective investor should carefully examine this Official Statement and 
its own financial condition to make a judgment as to its ability to bear the economic risk of such 
an investment, and whether or not the Bonds are an appropriate investment for such investor. 
Future Changes in Laws 
Various State and federal laws, regulations, and constitutional provisions apply to the City, 
the Bonds, the operation of the System and the authority of the City to impose and collect Service 
Charges with respect to the System. The City can give no assurance that there will not be a change 
in, interpretation of, or addition to such applicable laws, provisions and regulations which would 
have a material effect, either directly or indirectly, on the City, or the City's ability to impose or 
collect Service Charges. Many elements of local government finance, including the issuance of 
debt and the imposition and collection of Service Charges are controlled by State government. 
Future actions of the State may affect the overall financial conditions of the City and the ability of 
the City to impose and collect Service Charges, taxes or collect revenues for its ongoing operations. 
The City cannot predict whether, or in what form, any such change may be enacted into law, nor 
can the City predict the effect of any such change on the City's finances. 
Factors Relating to Tax Matters  
As discussed under "TAX MATTERS" herein, interest on the Bonds could become includible 
in gross income for purposes of federal income taxation, retroactive to the date the Bonds were 
issued, as a result of future acts or omissions of the City in violation of its covenants in the 
Indenture. Should such an event of taxability occur, the Bonds are not subject to any special 
redemption. 
There are or may be pending in the Congress of the United States legislative proposals 
relating to the federal tax treatment of interest on the Bonds, including some that carry retroactive 
effective dates, that, if enacted, could affect the market value of the Bonds. It cannot be predicted 
whether or in what form any such proposal might be enacted or whether, if enacted, it would apply 
to Bonds issued prior to enactment. Prospective purchasers of the Bonds should consult their own 
tax advisors regarding any pending or proposed federal tax legislation. Bond Counsel expresses 
no opinion regarding any pending or proposed federal tax legislation. Finally, reduction or 
elimination of the tax-exempt status of obligations such as the Bonds could have an adverse effect 
on the City's ability to access the capital markets to finance future capital or operational needs by 
reducing market demand for such obligations or materially increasing borrowing costs of the City. 
The tax-exempt bond office of the Internal Revenue Service (the "Service") is conducting 
audits of tax-exempt bonds, both compliance checks and full audits, with increasing frequency to  
35 
 
determine whether, in the view of the Service, interest on such tax-exempt obligations is includible 
in the gross income of the owners thereof for federal income tax purposes. It cannot be predicted 
whether the Service will commence any such audit. If an audit is commenced, under current 
procedures the Service may treat the City as a taxpayer and the bondholders may have no right to 
participate in such proceeding. The commencement of an audit with respect to any tax-exempt 
obligations of the City could adversely affect the market value and liquidity of the Bonds, 
regardless of the ultimate outcome. 
Bankruptcy 
Units of local government in Illinois, such as the City, cannot currently file for protection 
under the U.S. Bankruptcy Code unless specifically authorized to be a debtor by state law or by a 
governmental officer or organization empowered by state law to authorize such entity to be a 
debtor in a bankruptcy proceeding. State law does not currently permit the City to be a debtor in a 
bankruptcy proceeding. However, from time to time, legislation has been introduced in the Illinois 
General Assembly which, if enacted, would permit Illinois units of local government to be a debtor 
in bankruptcy under the U.S. Bankruptcy Code. The previous Governor of the State proposed 
legislation to allow for municipal bankruptcy, and legislation was introduced in the General 
Assembly to that effect, although it did not pass. The City cannot predict whether the Illinois 
General Assembly may adopt any future legislation that would permit units of local government, 
such as the City, to be a debtor in bankruptcy and the subsequent form and terms of any such 
proceeding. 
In rendering its opinion, Bond Counsel advises that the enforceability (but not the validity 
or binding effect) of the Bonds, the Indenture and the Second Supplemental Indenture (i) may be 
limited by any applicable bankruptcy, insolvency or other laws affecting the rights or remedies of 
creditors now or hereafter in effect and (ii) is subject to the principles of equity in the event that 
equitable remedies are sought, either in an action at law or in equity. 
LITIGATION 
The City is not engaged in and, to the best of its knowledge and belief, has not been 
threatened with, any litigation of any nature which seeks to restrain or enjoin the issuance, sale, 
execution or delivery of the Bonds or which in any way contests the validity of the Bonds or any 
proceedings of the City taken with respect to their issuance or sale or the pledge or application of 
any moneys or the security provided for the payment of the Bonds, or which contests the creation, 
organization or existence of the City or the title of any of the present members or other officials of 
the City to their respective offices. Upon the delivery of the Bonds, the City will deliver a 
certificate, in form satisfactory to Katten Muchin Rosenman LLP ("Bond Counsel"), to the effect 
of the foregoing. 
The City's Interim Corporation Counsel reports that any litigation and claims currently 
pending against the City are being handled by the City's insurance carrier, outside counsel or the 
City's Legal Department and will not affect the issuance of the Bonds. Such litigation is not 
expected to materially impact City finances.
